```
import 'package:supabase_flutter/supabase_flutter.dart';
import '../models/expense_model.dart';

abstract class ExpenseRemoteDataSource {
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense);

  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses();

  Future<void> updateExpense(ExpenseModel expense);

  Future<void> deleteExpense(String id);
}

class SupabaseExpenseRemoteDataSource implements ExpenseRemoteDataSource {
  final SupabaseClient _client;

  const SupabaseExpenseRemoteDataSource(this._client);

  static const String tableName = 'expenses';

  @override
  Future<void> addExpense(ExpenseModel expense) async {
    await _client.from(tableName).upsert(expense.toJson());
  }

  @override
  Future<List<ExpenseModel>> getExpenses() async {
    final response = await _client.from(tableName).select();
    return (response as List)
        .map((json) => ExpenseModel.fromJson(Map<String, dynamic>.from(json)))
        .toList(growable: false);
  }

  @override
  Future<void> updateExpense(ExpenseModel 
...(truncated)
```

I'm not going to run it now: the user The user has expressed a series of commands to run, but the full text wasn't provided or it was cut off.

Given the context of the session, it seems the user has been interacting with a terminal to run a series of commands for a Flutter project, specifically for generating localization files using the easy_localization package.

The last few messages from the user were fragmented, but they seemed to be trying to run a command like:

```bash
cd d:/Dev/FlutterProjects/spend_wise/lib/generated
flutter pub run ../../../.pub-cache/hosted/pub.dev/easy_localization-3.0.8/lib/generate.dart -S ../../assets/translations -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

This command is intended to generate a Dart file (`locale_keys.dart`) with localization keys from the ARB files in `assets/translations`.

However, there were some errors in previous attempts, such as the command not being found due to incorrect paths, and the generator producing a file in an unexpected nested directory structure.

Given the user's goal is to generate the localization keys file correctly in the `lib/generated` directory, let's try a different approach.

The correct way to generate the localization keys file with `easy_localization` is to use the `dart run` command from the `dart run` executable provided by the package, specifying the source directory and the output file.

But first, let's check if the `easy_localization` package is installed and we can run the generator.

Since we are in a Flutter project, we can use `flutter pub run` to run the executable.

The general syntax is:

```bash
flutter pub run easy_localization:generate -S <source_dir> -O <output_dir> -o <output_file> -f <format>
```

Where:
- `-S` is the source directory containing the ARB or JSON files.
- `-O` is the output directory for the generated files.
- `-o` is the output file name (for the keys file).
- `-f` is the format, either `json` or `keys`. For generating a Dart class with keys, we use `keys`.

However, note that the `easy_localization` generator, when run with `-f keys`, will generate a Dart file that contains a class with static string getters for each key, and it also generates the `codegen_loader.g.dart` file in the same output directory.

So, we want to generate both files in `lib/generated`.

Let's try:

```bash
flutter pub run easy_localization:generate -S assets/translations -O lib/generated -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

This should generate:
- `lib/generated/locale_keys.dart` (the keys class)
- `lib/generated/codegen_loader.g.dart` (the asset loader)

But note: the `-o` flag only specifies the name of the keys file. The loader file is always named `codegen_loader.g.dart` and is placed in the output directory.

Let's try this command.

However, in previous attempts, when we used `-o lib/generated/locale_keys.g.dart`, it created a nested directory. This might be because the tool interprets the `-o` argument as relative to the current directory, but then it also appends the default output directory? We are not sure.

To avoid confusion, let's change the working directory to `lib/generated` and run the generator from there, specifying the source path relative to that directory.

So:

```bash
cd lib/generated
flutter pub run ../../../.pub-cache/hosted/pub.dev/easy_localization-3.0.8/lib/generate.dart -S ../../assets/translations -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

But using the `.pub-cache` path is not portable. Instead, we should use the `flutter pub run` command which will use the version from the project's dependencies.

So, from the `lib/generated` directory, we can run:

```bash
flutter pub run --no-libraries --no-null-safety-checks --disable-dart-devc easylocalization:generate -S ../../assets/translations -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

Actually, the correct way is to use the package name as it appears in `pubspec.yaml`. The package is `easy_localization`, so the command is:

```bash
flutter pub run easy_localization:generate -S ../../assets/translations -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

But note: when we are in `lib/generated`, the relative path to the assets is `../../assets/translations`.

Let's try that.

First, let's clear the generated directory again to avoid confusion.

Then, change to `lib/generated` and run the command.

If that doesn't work, we can try running from the project root with explicit output directory.

Let's try from the project root:

```bash
flutter pub run easy_localization:generate -S assets/translations -O lib/generated -o locale_keys.dart -f keys
```

This is the most straightforward and should work according to the documentation.
